Miscellaneous Writings on Xingsheng Street 219

— Fan Xuehui

Xingsheng Street, if people have no connection to it, of course they won't know it, but I believe those women will not be without an impression of it; because this is indeed the only small street in Shanghai that sells wool yarn, so there are also the most wool yarn shops here, and there are also quite a few paint shops in addition. This narrow street, in terms of its commercial position in the French Concession, is probably one of the best.

Every spring, merchants from the mainland come to Shanghai to buy goods, and it is essential for them to come here, as commodities such as wool yarn and paint can probably only be sold here, and are not easy to find elsewhere.

So at that time, there were Jiangbei merchants wearing melon skin hats and blue long gowns, who were foolish and simple. There are merchants from Jiangsu and Zhejiang who are slick in their actions and articulate. There are also northern merchants who are generous in their wheel prices and have eccentric tempers who come here to buy goods.

When the north wind howls, deep autumn is about to pass, and the god in charge of winter comes with severe cold. At that time, the scene on Xingsheng Street seems to have changed its face again, like the Women's Kingdom in "Flowers in the Mirror," coming and going, bustling with women. This is the time to buy wool yarn and make winter clothes. There are bourgeois women, young female students in teams of three or five carrying small leather briefcases. There are female workers, and so-called artistic actors and stars also come, as well as Pudong-style women who carry vegetables in the morning and sell them along the street.

They squeeze into the doorways of every wool yarn shop, take the wool yarn, and slowly deliberate on which color is suitable for themselves. By the night of the re-emergence of spring, this place has also returned to its original appearance.

I have stepped into this small street for more than ten years. In the past, they were very simple, but now, every wool yarn shop has actually installed a three-dimensional large glass window, displaying colorful and eye-catching wool yarn. This is undoubtedly an image of commercial competition and economic bankruptcy.

In the past few days, this place has been filled with shouting and noise all day long. After the god of night pulls the gray veil together, it gradually becomes quiet; but the music and singing of the dancing hall on Zhu Bao San Road occupy our eardrums again.

Changing Nest and Mating Phoenix 220

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Eighth Episode: Vows Exchanged Over a Cup of Water, Faded Thoughts Under the Green Lamp; Gold-Embroidered Fingers Declare Yearning with Red Beans

This was too good; his bitterness had finally come to an end. He didn't hide from his friend and was willing to give him something that symbolized love between a man and a woman. If this continued, he would surely reach the pinnacle of love. He had already forgotten the heat and wore the ring on his little finger, then slowly stroked it with his hand. He didn't know how long he had been imagining this, but when he looked up out the window, the sun was already gone from the courtyard. He felt extremely happy at this moment, feeling that everything in the universe was lovely. It wasn't too hot, so he decided to visit his friend and have a good talk. He didn't hesitate, put on his long gown and straw hat, and went out. The ring on his little finger wasn't removed either. On the street, he looked at every young man he saw, wondering if they were engaged or married. If they weren't engaged, they couldn't imagine the joy of being engaged. When he saw women, he thought that he didn't need to envy them anymore, because the most beautiful, virtuous, and capable woman in the world belonged to him. As he thought this, a smile kept appearing on his face. People on the road saw his expression and couldn't figure out what was wrong with this young man. He was very refined and composed, so why was he smiling while walking? He himself didn't understand any of this, he just kept walking. When he felt a bit more open space in front of him, he looked up and saw a row of city walls, and below the walls, a vegetable garden. In it were two ponds with tall reeds, and a few sparse willows with two pavilions nestled among them. Oh, this was Bailuzhou (White Heron Isle) in the east of the city. Why had he come here? He looked at the sky again and saw red clouds on half the sky, reflecting off the blue sky in the pond. Crows were constantly flying across the sky. Well, it wouldn't hurt to play around at Bailuzhou. The evening scenery was very beautiful. As he walked, he wondered if he was being too happy. Maybe there was a reason for this. Would Menglan really ask Youmei to handle such a secret matter? Besides, Youmei had never mentioned it before. And today's attitude was also suspicious. This change of mind made him feel disheartened, so he decided not to visit Bailuzhou and turned around to head back. He had been very relaxed when he came, but now he walked extremely fast on the way back. When he got home, it was naturally dark, and the lamp was lit. Under the lamplight, it was very clear that a copper ruler was holding down a letter. The bottom of the letter said "Today," and was signed "MN." Could this already be a key, unlocking Guoqi's lock of worries? He didn't sit down at the time, but impatiently started reading. (104)

Suzhou Creek 221

— Jiao Shijie

Cutting across the middle of Shanghai, from east to west, this winding stream of water, as black as mud, meanders and twists, dividing Shanghai into two areas: the south bank is the Concession, and the north bank is called Zhabei. It also separates two classes of people. Those who live in the Concession are mostly wealthy merchants, rich gentlemen, extravagant young masters, and fashionable beautiful girls. These are considered the upper class(?). Those who live in Zhabei are common laborers, hardworking workers, peddlers, and drifters. They live in thatched huts and eat simple food like pancakes and sweet potatoes, which is, of course, not comparable to the upper class(?) people who live in Western-style houses in the Concession and eat fine food. Therefore, they can only be called the lower class! However, in this lower-class area, the forces of a certain kind of people are lurking, constantly showing affection and threatening. The poor people are crying out in pain. This seems to divide the classes even more clearly. On this river, countless boats come and go every day. The whistling sound of small steamships and the black smoke constantly fill the river. This is the Suzhou Creek that everyone in Shanghai knows.

The Suzhou Creek enjoys great fame due to its location, but after the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, it divided the war zone and the non-war zone, making its position even more important and its reputation doubled. The current Suzhou Creek is like an ancient "moat." During the January 28th Incident, Zhabei was reduced to scorched earth, while the south of the Suzhou Creek remained untouched. Refugees who escaped across the Suzhou Creek felt like they had reached a safe haven. Life and death were separated by just one river. At that time, the Suzhou Creek could be called the "River of Life and Death."

There are more than a dozen bridges on the Suzhou Creek. The most modern and grand steel bridge is the Waibaidu Bridge (Garden Bridge) and the Old Rubbish Bridge. Countless trams and cars pass over them every day, yet they remain unmoved. It is difficult to estimate how much pressure they can withstand. Other steel and concrete bridges include the Libaidu Bridge, Sichuan Road Bridge, Tianhougong Bridge, and New Rubbish Bridge, all lying quietly on the river. The other wooden bridges are also quite sturdy and can bear the responsibility of transportation, fulfilling their duties happily!

The eastern end of the Suzhou Creek connects with the Huangpu River. On the left is a twenty-story building, and on the right is the Bund Park, like two giant stone lions guarding the entrance, decorating the Suzhou Creek in a spectacular way. At the intersection of Sichuan Road is the Shanghai Postal Administration, dark and majestic, with an ancient atmosphere. Especially in the area east of the Xinzha Bridge, many tall buildings are banks' warehouses and depots. On the banks of the river, like a long snake formation, are arranged dung carts, and a peculiar stench spreads with the flow of air.

West of the Xinzha Bridge, it gradually transitions into a slum area. Here are small thatched huts, huddled together with families of men and women, most of whom are from Jiangbei. The men make a living by pulling rickshaws, and the women go out to do needlework, mending clothes and socks for others. The children also work collecting garbage. In the hot summer, you can see naked children, like Little Sanzi and Little Liuzi. In winter, they shiver in the northwest wind. All year round, the stench of the river, the smell of feces, and the smell of people constantly enter their breath.

Such is the scenery on the Suzhou Creek.

Xujiahui at Dusk 222

— Xiafei

In the evening, shrouded in the setting sun, we dragged three uneven shadows, swaying and staggering back to Xujiahui. It was a place not far from the city but with a touch of rural flavor. There, we could see many dilapidated thatched huts in slums, and also villas with small Western-style houses. There were churches, schools, young male and female students, children picking up dead branches, leisurely gentlemen, wives, young masters, and young ladies; there were crowds struggling below in hell, preachers carrying crosses, unemployed people wandering in the streets, fat heads, hungry faces: There was… this other side of the city, a convergence of joy, suffering, tranquility, and noise.

The leaves of the French plane trees fluttered in the air like flying butterflies. Two or three tourists loitered by the roadside, but their faces seemed a bit melancholy. The roof of the church stood tall like two pen tips. The setting sun shone on the cross on the spire, emitting a metallic glow that trembled in the air.

Just as we circled around the church, suddenly a strange smell wafted over from the evening breeze. We quickly covered our noses and fled into a narrow alley. The green shade overhead in that vertical narrow alley blocked the sky, and the twilight of the setting sun slipped in, creating a Western oil painting-like color tone.

After passing through Tushanwan, we crossed a small bridge and seemed to enter a desolate village. The surrounding area was all fields, although there were some clusters of village houses, and even flowing water, plank bridges, dogs barking, and chickens crowing, but it seemed sparsely populated. In front of the Lianhua Film Company's studio, a large group of people were gathered, craning their necks to look at the sky. So, we also curiously looked up at the sky, and saw a small object climbing very fast in the blue sky. Its tail seemed to be spitting out a white smoke, and it instantly formed four English letters: C.N.A.C.

"Airplane writing." I remembered seeing something like an aerial advertisement in some foreign films, where a small airplane flew in the sky and wrote smoke letters.

Next to the Lianhua studio, we took the opportunity to visit the Asian Bee Farm and talked a lot about beekeeping experiences with General Deng Bingshan. He said: Beekeeping is indeed a sideline that urgently needs to be promoted in our country, especially near orchards, because it is not only beneficial to flowers and fruits, but also because of the abundance of honey sources, the honey production is also excellent. In modern times, honey has a wide range of uses. No matter in candy, medicine, cosmetics, or cigarettes, honey is indispensable. According to current customs statistics, the annual import of foreign honey amounts to millions, but our country is still missing out on the benefits of this great sideline. Coming out of the Asian Bee Farm, we originally wanted to visit the Lianhua studio, but it was too late, so we looked for the road back home.

"The setting sun is infinitely good, it's just near dusk." I felt infinite nostalgia and regret for this vast spring scenery!

Shen Bao Medical and Pharmaceutical Supplement

Random Notes on the Family Hygiene Status of Villagers in the Qimei Road Civilian Village, Shanghai 223

— Li Caihua

I.

The term "Civilian Village" is familiar to people, right? It is one of the constructions of Greater Shanghai. The Qimei Road Civilian Village is in a corner of the Shanghai countryside, but its economic structure is still inseparable from the economic structure of the metropolis of Shanghai; therefore, every movement is closely related. I have written two articles, one is the statistics of children's deaths, published in this newspaper in June, and the other is a survey of women recently published in the Central Daily News. What I want to write now is the family hygiene status of the villagers, because the goodness of family hygiene is closely related to the health of each member of the family. A hygienic family can directly promote the well-being of the family population and the soundness of the family organization; indirectly, it can help to consolidate the foundation of the country and cure a part of the diseases of the society. If we want to improve their family life, we must pay attention to family hygiene.

II.

There are a total of two hundred and fifty families in our village. According to the length of time the households have lived here, some have just moved in, and some have moved in since February of this year! In the past ten months, we have been investigating their family hygiene status before they moved into the village, while also paying attention to their current family hygiene status, and at the same time implementing hygiene education. Now, I will summarize it into two parts: one is the family hygiene status outside the village (referring to before moving into the village), and the other is the family hygiene status inside the village (referring to after moving into the village, including new and old households).

III.

(I) Family Hygiene Status Outside the Village

According to the reports of the village households' conversations and the results of the survey, the following is the case:

(1) Those living in front buildings account for 7%, back buildings account for 13%, kitchen sheds account for 41%, attic rooms account for 33%, and back living rooms account for 6%. (2) Those living in the concessions (public concession) account for 67%, and those in the city (Zhabei) account for 33%. (3) Those with rent of four to six yuan account for more than 80%, and those with rent of seven to twelve yuan account for less than 20%. (4) They do not fold quilts or tidy beds. (5) The furniture and objects in the room are messy. (6) Snot and phlegm can be seen everywhere. (7) The room is small and crowded, the air is stifled, and there is little sunlight. (8) The kitchen, bedroom, and toilet are connected together. (9) Doors and windows are often closed. (10) The tables and chairs are covered with dust, and fruit peels and paper scraps are thrown everywhere. (11) The whole family sleeps in one room.

Looking at the above report, we can draw the following conclusions:

Items 4, 5, 6, 9, and 10 are habit problems; the rest are economic problems.

(II) Family Hygiene Status Inside the Village

We will analyze the family hygiene status inside the village based on the above two conclusions.

First, let's talk about economic problems—it can be said that there are no problems anymore. The appearance and interior of the Class A and Class B residences in this village are the same throughout the village. The bedroom, living room, kitchen, storage room, and toilet are all clearly separated. The direction of the houses is uniformly facing south, naturally with plenty of sunlight. There are large sports fields, wide roads, and various new-style sanitary facilities here, so the problems caused by economics are no longer problems.

As for habit problems—indeed, the newly arrived villagers still have unhygienic habits. We often see that when they first move in, the ground is covered with fruit peels, paper scraps, and phlegm. The placement of furniture and objects is also inappropriate; the quilts and clothes on the bed are often piled together in a mess; the doors and windows are always tightly closed; and there are still traces of dust on the tables and chairs. In short, it is not much different from the unhygienic situation outside the village. However, after two or three months, it is different, and this is not without reason:

(1) There is a group life—the families are very connected, and the feelings are becoming increasingly close, unlike when they lived outside the village, where tenants in the same residence rarely interacted. Here, the Zhang family goes to the Li family, the Li family goes to the Wang family, new households go to old households, and old households go to new households, coming and going frequently. An assimilation effect and competitive psychology have developed invisibly; therefore, unhygienic habits have also been reduced a lot invisibly. This is the first reason.

(2) Infusion of hygiene education—we often hold hygiene education lectures, fully infusing common hygiene knowledge; we also constantly post popular hygiene slogans, pictures, and distribute leaflets, thus increasing their deep understanding of improving family hygiene. This is the second reason.

(3) Cleanliness inspection—we often go to their homes to chat and secretly check the cleanliness. When we encounter unhygienic situations, we give earnest advice. Therefore, going to their homes more often means creating more opportunities for them to improve. The more opportunities, the more significant the improvement. This is the third reason.

IV.

As for the old households, the family hygiene status is improving day by day; at the same time, most have changed their past unhygienic habits, but the new households have not achieved this. In the future, we will let the old households take on the important responsibility of persuasion and propaganda. We will use this part of our time and energy to study how to improve the villagers' family life methods.

At the same time, I would like to tell the readers: when they lived outside the village, they often got sick. I think this is absolutely related to the quality of family hygiene, and it is directly proportional: to put it clearly, unhealthy families definitely have more sick people, and healthy families definitely have fewer sick people. If we were to investigate the material losses suffered by each family member nationwide due to illness, then this statistical math would definitely be very alarming.

We dare not be complacent because, due to the limitations of manpower and financial resources, we are still far from our ideal. Here, I sincerely and devoutly hope that those who care about social issues will always give their advice and guidance.

The Problem of Building the Nursing Profession in China Tomorrow (Part 2) 224

— Li Lingdong

Therefore, if we want to reform nursing education and raise the nursing profession, we must start with the construction of the nursing education system. After graduating from senior nursing vocational schools, there can still be opportunities for further study. The establishment of academies for studying one's own career will make the nursing profession a specialized academic institution. Therefore, the establishment of nursing colleges or university-affiliated nursing departments, and various academic departments to study specialized fields, such as nursing administration, nursing technology, nursing education, nursing nutrition, public health nursing, psychiatric nursing, etc.

In this way, there will be no need for us to shout loudly that nursing is sacred and great. Colleagues engaged in the nursing profession will not despise themselves or have the distorted idea of wanting to become doctors. Society will no longer have the mistaken perception of "high-class tea servants," "caregivers," "nursing women," or "the most economical laborers in hospitals." The nursing profession is a specialized technology and a profession with profound knowledge that protects human health. This nursing education system, which urgently needs to be built and laid the foundation for, still hopes to achieve success as soon as possible in the initial sound of reforming nursing education, and establish a top nursing academy to raise the social status of the nursing profession.

Third, the establishment of nursing supervisors is an essential element of a sound organization.

When nursing education is being planned, the highest administrative organ of nursing education spares no effort to engage in construction and transformation for the development of nursing careers, planning and all facilities, to complete the ideal Chinese nursing career.

However, for this great construction project of the Chinese nursing career, how can the higher-level organs plan perfectly and design the implementation, if only relying on the higher-level organs? However, the unit that bears the mission of completing the nurse's new education – the nursing school. If they do not work according to the regulations and truly implement the new education, then it still cannot help the overall situation. Why do we only talk about the importance of nursing schools and not about the nurse's professional problems in society or the nurse's professional problems in hospitals? Because nursing school is the place for training nursing talents, the basic source of the nursing career. If there are defects in the cell organization of nursing students, even if they grow into an individual and become a successful nurse, they will still be a nurse with an unsound body and mind, harming the community. Therefore, the construction of nursing schools is extremely important for the construction of the nursing career. Then, is there supervision of whether nursing schools are working reliably? We can also answer without a doubt that it is an even more important matter.

Therefore, the establishment of the nursing supervisor system is to supervise whether nursing schools are working thoroughly and sincerely, a prescription of the right medicine for the disease. Because often higher-level authorities have strict and comprehensive business plans, but lower-level subordinates often feign compliance and do not implement the work according to the promulgated procedures, some are confused, and some are fraudulent. All the work becomes written articles, written reports, and higher-level organs cannot know the situation and have no way to investigate. Work efficiency and business progress will never reach the day of development, so the function of the establishment of nursing supervisors should be generated according to needs, which can connect the upper and lower parties, communicate them, and increase administrative efficiency. The importance of the supervisory system is evident in this respect, and it is indeed a problem worth studying.

Fourth, the reform of the nursing curriculum is the blueprint for the construction project.

Regarding the curriculum reform issue, the first step is to discuss the nursing school nursing student ward internship problem. Nursing student ward internships are more important than any other vocational school internship because the object of the nursing profession is to seek the happiness of patients and relieve their suffering. Occasional negligence in the details will cause the patient's life to suffer great sacrifice. Therefore, the entire technology that is learned must be practiced, practiced, and observed in the ward, to learn how to engage in nursing work and procedures.

However, what is the current situation of nursing student internships? Most of them are working in the ward while studying. In the earliest grades, the internship time is three or four hours a day, and then gradually increases. The higher the grade, the more time is spent, or even more than ten hours a day. We have always opposed this system because it contains great malpractices and dangers.

Because when working in the ward, the work encountered has not yet been taught in the curriculum. The efficacy, method, and disadvantages of this technology are not known at all. We ask nursing students to implement this technology to serve patients. We think that if they do this blindly, patients will not get the benefit of the technical value, and nursing students will not be able to achieve the purpose of learning to work.

Also, due to the allocation of class time, coming and going to the ward, the situation of the ward work and the progress of the patient's symptoms cannot be thoroughly understood. Re-examining the study of medical records cannot show the spirit of nurse service, or their loyalty to their work. Therefore, it is uneconomical in terms of time, and there is no possibility of progress in the learning efficiency of nursing students.

Page 20

Joining the Shantytowns of the Jiangsu Provincial Capital to Administer Vaccinations (Continued) 225

— Yin Baishui

(4) Superstition runs deep. People believe that by hanging a red cloth strip on their heads with the words "Smallpox Passed" written on it and praying a few words before a wooden idol, they can avoid smallpox and are unwilling to get vaccinated.

(5) They believe that vaccination can trigger fetal toxins, so children are always vaccinated only when they are three or four years old. They also say that in children under two years old, fetal toxins cannot be released.

(6) They believe that because it is a charitable endeavor, the vaccine must not be of high quality, and they often refuse to accept it. In families with limited means, they also feel uneasy about something that is free, not realizing that everyone has already contributed to these medical expenses, and everyone has the benefit of receiving free vaccinations.

(7) When they are unwilling to accept vaccinations, no matter how long you talk, they will still lower their heads, doing their work, or answer "Yes... Yes..." perfunctorily, perhaps not even hearing what you are saying. If you continue to talk, you might just get a cold shoulder.

(8) In this rising tide of rural bankruptcy and increasing unemployment, the general lower classes are truly too poor. They cannot survive without working, and it is not easy to achieve even basic sustenance. Add to that their stubborn thinking that vaccination requires eating "hot" foods and avoiding certain foods. Where would they get the money to buy these "hot" foods? Therefore, they make excuses and are unwilling to be vaccinated.

(9) In private schools crowded with many children, when you contact them about vaccination, before you finish speaking, the teachers always say without thinking: "...You are truly working hard, coming out to vaccinate people in this cold weather. It's truly a kind gesture, but all the students here have already been vaccinated. Thank you for your kindness..." Are they telling the truth? If you ask them further, they might say, "However, we can't get schools here, the students can't get vaccinated themselves because their parents entrust the children to my care, and I bear a great responsibility. If you insist on vaccinating these children, feel free, but let me notify their parents tonight. Those who are willing to be vaccinated can then notify you, and then we will bother you!" Do they really go to each parent to encourage vaccination? Will they notify you later? Many untrained private school teachers only know how to teach children dead knowledge, placing the children's health far beyond their concerns.

Insights from Research

(1) Before vaccination, explain that cowpox vaccination does not require avoiding certain foods or eating "hot" foods. This can dispel the mindset of those who are poor and cannot afford "hot" foods and are therefore unwilling to get vaccinated.

(2) When making rounds for vaccination, it is advisable to use the pressure-prick method (using a needle to prick the epidermis to allow the vaccine to enter). This is because the equipment is easy to sterilize and economical. Using the mouth to blow the vaccine onto the skin is unhygienic. You can use a five-fen long rubber tube, pierce a small hole, cut off both ends of the vaccine, insert one end into the small hole in the rubber tube, and firmly close both ends of the rubber tube with your thumb and index finger, applying pressure to squeeze it. The air pressure in the tube will force the vaccine out from the other end.

(3) Everyone has a fear of pain, so this is especially important to pay attention to when vaccinating in large groups. If the first person says that vaccination is very painful, no second or third person will volunteer to be vaccinated. Therefore, the first person to be vaccinated should be someone more knowledgeable and robust. Before the injection, use people's competitive nature to first encourage their courage, for example, saying, "You are very brave. Actually, vaccination doesn't hurt at all, it's lighter than a mosquito bite! If you say it hurts, that person is too timid." After such suggestion and encouragement, even if it is painfully uncomfortable, they will endure it themselves, so they will pretend that it doesn't hurt, and will even automatically encourage others. Moreover, the actual vaccination is not as painful as an injection.

(4) The number of vaccinated men accounts for more than two-thirds, among which the number of women being vaccinated for the first time exceeds the number of revaccinations. The opposite is true for men. (Referring to shantytowns.)

(5) The age of vaccinated people: there are more people under ten years old than over ten years old. For women, the ratio of those over ten years old to those under ten years old is 1 to 10. For men, the ratio of those over ten years old to those under ten years old is 4 to 6. (Referring to shantytowns.)

(6) If people are unwilling to be vaccinated due to the cold weather and intend to get vaccinated in the spring of next year, if the advantages and disadvantages can be explained in detail, they can generally be persuaded to be vaccinated.

(7) For people who do not believe in vaccination and are blindly superstitious, even after a lot of time and detailed explanation, the results are still very small. Moreover, after you leave, they will still grumble and curse you for a while.

Concluding Remarks

The Jiangsu Provincial Capital has now started administering cowpox vaccinations, not only in the streets and markets but also extended to the lower-class shantytown areas. This spirit is worthy of admiration. It is hoped that other places will also start soon to eliminate traces of smallpox. Even then, we have not achieved what we hoped. Look again! In rural villages without sanitation facilities, the incidence of various infectious diseases is higher than in cities, and the mortality rate is very high, which is truly a danger to our country. Therefore, it is even more hoped that the health authorities will extend the work of administering cowpox vaccinations to rural villages where knowledge is shallow, superstition is deep, thinking is stubborn, and there are no sanitation facilities, so that every farmer can receive its benefits and get its protection. That is the fortune of our country's farmers, and it is what I have been yearning for and praying for day and night. (The End)

Domestic Medicinal Plants (Continued) 226

— Zhou Mengbai

Borage Family Borraginaceae Purple Gromwell Lithospermum officinale, L. var. erythrorhizon, Maxim. (L. erythrorhizon Sieb. et Zucc.)

(Plant) Grows naturally in the mountains and fields; a perennial herb. The stem reaches a height of 30-60 cm. The leaves are alternate, sessile, lanceolate, entire, with acuminate tips. Axillary or terminal racemose inflorescences appear, bearing white and shallowly lobed small funnel-shaped flowers in summer. The nut is an ovoid particle.

(Crude Drug) Purple Root Radix Lithospermi, which is collected from its roots and dried. This product is irregular and branched, 10-50 cm long and 0.5-1.0 cm in diameter. The cortex is dark purple, with significant wrinkles, and the material is thin and easily peeled off. When a piece of this product is put into a small amount of Ether or Benzene, it immediately turns a beautiful violet color. A General Overview of the Work of the China Anti-Tuberculosis Association Over the Past Three Years and Future Plans (Continued from Issue 201) 227

— Yan Fuqing

(9) Raising funds to build a sanatorium – Shanghai has a population of over 3.5 million, and based on statistics, the number of people suffering from tuberculosis is estimated to be around 200,000. However, there are fewer than 500 tuberculosis beds in all the hospitals in the city. Such a large city cannot even find a tuberculosis sanatorium. Patients suffering from tuberculosis have the suffering of having no place to be treated. In view of this, the Association has repeatedly wanted to raise funds to build a tuberculosis sanatorium. However, the cost is huge, and due to the economic downturn, it has not been successful. This year, we are pleased to celebrate Mr. Yu Qiaqing's 70th birthday. Mr. Yu generously donated the income from his birthday celebration as funds for the construction of the Qiaqing Anti-Tuberculosis Hospital. With the efforts of Mayor Wu and others, funds have now been raised. The Shanghai Medical Affairs Committee has also donated land for the hospital's construction, and the construction is expected to start in the near future.

(10) Organizing branches in various places – If we want to achieve effective tuberculosis prevention, it is essential to establish anti-tuberculosis branches in various places. Due to its limited manpower, the Association cannot send people to organize branches in various places. Therefore, this work does not yet have a proper starting point. However, it continues to strive to contact local gentry to organize branches. Currently, the efforts are focusing on Fuzhou, Changsha, Suzhou, Hangzhou, Guangzhou, Nanjing, Beiping, and other places. In the future, once the anti-tuberculosis associations in various places are successfully organized, the reduction in the tuberculosis mortality rate can be anticipated.

The above is a general overview of the work of the Association over the past three years. Due to space limitations, I can only briefly report as above. Other matters, such as the establishment of the Shanghai Anti-Tuberculosis Committee, the expansion of the Association's office, the contact and gathering of members, personnel changes, internal renovation, and the organization of various committees (such as the Medical Affairs Committee, Editorial Committee, and Promotion Committee), cannot be described in detail here. It is hoped that people from all walks of life will understand.

It is not easy to say what the Association's plans are for the next three years. During these three years, various circumstances may limit and make it difficult to make definite decisions. However, we already know that the past three years have been a period of promotional work, that is, a period of educational work. This has allowed society to have a reasonable understanding of tuberculosis prevention and control. This type of promotion is extremely important. However, if work is only promotional without practical action, it cannot arouse social interest or win the trust of the public. It is like opening a store and only advertising without goods. Once citizens go to buy, there is no way to meet their needs. This failure is inevitable. Therefore, the Association's work plan for the next three years should use practical work to prove the necessity and true meaning of the Association's existence.

The implementation method should be based on which aspects have the most achievements and meet the needs of the people, so as to benefit the public.

Establishment of Children's Health Camps

We deeply know that tuberculosis is the most easily transmitted disease. The transmission of pulmonary tuberculosis in the world is faster than any other disease, and more harmful than diseases such as leprosy and cholera. According to recent medical research, pulmonary tuberculosis is extremely easy to transmit from youth to childhood, whether in the milk of humans, cows, and sheep, or in other foods or air. Therefore, children are most susceptible to tuberculosis. According to statistics, from infancy to twelve years old, 80% or 90% have tuberculosis roots. However, sometimes because of stronger physical strength, it does not expand, but if there is a loss of balance or improper protection, it can run rampant. Therefore, attention should be paid to preventing transmission. Therefore, the establishment of children's health camps is more time- and cost-effective, and children benefit more. This is the first plan for the future.

Addition of Clinics

Secondly, clinics should be gradually established. The Association has now set up two clinics. Based on experience, it is more cost-effective to run more. For example, if the cost of running one is 3,000, then running two is only 4,000. If two are planned each year, then six can be added in three years? These clinics must be made universal, that is, methods should be found to establish them in the public concession and the French concession. The main purposes of establishing clinics are: (1) to allow people with mild illnesses to come to the clinic for examination. This work is more effective than hospital treatment, because tuberculosis is extremely difficult to treat in the second and third stages, but it is very easy to treat in the first stage. Prevention is more effective than treatment. Establishing more clinics makes citizens understand the importance of tuberculosis examination and makes it convenient; (2) to allow healthy young people to come to the clinic nearby for physical examinations, so that they know whether they are healthy or have an infection. The development of this outpatient clinic should be promoted as much as possible in three years.

Running Tuberculosis Sanatoriums

Thirdly, running tuberculosis sanatoriums. According to investigations, there are only 350 pulmonary beds in all of Shanghai. If compared with the population and the prevalence of tuberculosis, 3,500 would still not be enough. Therefore, there is an urgent need to establish these sanatoriums. Now, a hospital with 50 beds has been established in Jiangwan, but there are already more than 200 registered people. Therefore, even wealthy people who have contracted tuberculosis and want to find a place for recuperation still find it difficult! However, the cost of running sanatoriums is relatively high, and should be implemented based on economic capacity.

Promoting Health Exercises

Fourthly, promoting health exercises. We recall that after the war in Europe, the French army's fatigue resulted in a large increase in tuberculosis patients. Therefore, promoting health exercises to enhance resistance in the next three years of tuberculosis prevention is also a priority.

China now is not the China of ten years ago. The Association's future is to prove whether our organization can exist through work; it is definitely not just relying on promotion. We must offer facts for donations received, and the government and people must unite and work together. At the same time, we should also seek young members to engage in practical work as the most important thing, and economic problems are secondary. (The End)

Special Telegraph Supplement

Shortwave

Telegraph Delivery Certificate 229

— Lü Bing

The telegraph office is a public service organization. Those who work in the telegraph office, whether they are staff or messengers, can be regarded as public servants. The only creed that public servants should adhere to in their duties is loyalty; with loyal public servants and loyal actions, there can be sufficient proof to gain public trust.

It has become a social custom for Chinese people not to send telegrams unless it is important. Therefore, each time a telegram is sent, it is particularly important, and the hope that it will reach its destination quickly is understandable, and the hope that it will be delivered to the recipient is also understandable. There are probably not a few senders who are concerned about their telegram while it is being transmitted. Is the telegraph office, which serves the public, truly loyal? Or do people sometimes harbor doubts?

To resolve this doubt and to let the owner of the telegram know as early as possible that the telegram has indeed reached the hands of the recipient, the only way is to notify the original sender when the original telegram arrives, or to send back the recipient's receipt. This method will be implemented from today, and is called the "Telegraph Delivery Notification."

The delivery notification can also be called a telegraph delivery certificate. This certificate has two major significances: first, does the telegraph office transmit telegrams faithfully and deliver them properly? Looking at this certificate, the truth is clear. Second, how fast is the telegram transmitted? Can it meet the sender's expectations? With this delivery certificate, it can be used for investigation.

In fact, the transmission of telegrams, except in special circumstances (the so-called special circumstances, such as military periods, congested telegraph services, or line obstacles, and long-distance retransmissions), usually takes the shortcut, and is sent as soon as it arrives, with very little delay. However, although this is the case in reality, senders often inevitably have many concerns, because they have no absolute proof of speed. From now on, doubts can be dispelled, and anxiety is unnecessary. Just add the words "Return Receipt" before the text of the telegram, and soon you will be able to receive proof of delivery to relieve your concerns. The telegraph office serves the public, and the adoption of this method is not only for the sender's sake, but also provides faithful proof of the telegraph office's performance of its duties.

Reading "Telecommunications and Transportation and Transportation Construction" 230

— Zhen

Yesterday, I read Mr. Lin Diffei's "Telecommunications and Transportation and Transportation Construction" in the social service column of the Jiangxi Min Guo Daily on November 6. The article discussed the recent case in which the Guangchang Telegraph Branch presented a complaint, accusing the highway authority of opening business telephone services between Shangfeng, Nancheng, Guangchang, and Ningdu, and the Guangchang County Government telephone exchange of connecting with local agencies to make telephone calls, which harmed the telegraph branch's telephone business revenue. The telegram branch requested that the Telecommunications Administration relay the matter to the provincial government for strict prohibition. Mr. Lin, with an objective attitude, spoke a word for the telecommunications authorities. The attention of people from all walks of life to the telecommunications industry can be described as a good sign for sorting out the future.

The main points of Mr. Lin's article can be summarized as follows: (1) Telephone transportation is not explicitly stipulated as the monopoly of the telecommunications business, and is also not allowed by national politics and human economic behavior. (2) The telegraph office is a national transportation agency and should not be profit-oriented. (3) The Guangchang Telegraph Branch's telephone business charges excessive fees and is not economical in terms of time. (4) The Guangchang Telegraph Branch should not be greedy for credit and make false reports to hinder the development of transportation construction. The points mentioned seem to be reasonable, and it is feared that Mr. Lin is not the only one who holds such views. However, from the standpoint of the state-owned telecommunications business, there is indeed value in discussing it. The author does not know the ins and outs of this case, nor how the Jiangxi telecommunications authorities handled it. I would like to present it to Mr. Lin and people from all walks of life in the spirit of a third party, based on legal principles:

(1) According to the Telecommunications Regulations promulgated by the National Government on August 5, 1929, Article 2 states, "All telecommunications operated by the state shall be managed by the Ministry of Transportation of the Executive Yuan of the National Government; however, the army, navy, and air force agencies shall be responsible for military purposes. The self-built ones are not subject to this rule." The following telecommunications in Article 3 may be established by local governments, public-private organizations, or individuals after approval by the Ministry of Transportation of the Executive Yuan of the National Government or its entrusted agencies: ... (1) Those dedicated to railways, mines, or other special businesses: (2) Those used for Deesignating purposes when ships and aircraft are sailing; (3) Those who connect with local telecommunications agencies to communicate for the convenience of map transmission and reception: (4) Those dedicated to communication within the scope of a house lot: (5) Those dedicated to broadcasting news, lectures, weather, music, and songs that are beneficial to the public: (6) Those used for academic trial tests: (7) Establish telephones in a certain area where there is no telephone connection." Furthermore, according to the revised organizational law of the Ministry of Transportation promulgated by the National Government in February 1931, the regulations on the jurisdiction of administrative matters stipulated by the third Central Executive Committee at its second plenary session in October 1929, and the order of the Executive Yuan No. 385 on January 10, 1929, transferring and approving the order of the National Government on the telephone business to be handled by the Ministry of Transportation, as well as Article 19 of the KMT's internal policy platform, it has long been explicitly stipulated by the highest party and government authorities that the telephone business should be under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Transportation. The so-called "national politics and human economic behavior do not allow" is based on something that seems unfounded.

(2) State-owned telephone businesses should not be profit-oriented, which is the opinion of informed people, and is also the policy that the Ministry of Transportation is currently vigorously pursuing. However, for decades, China's telecommunications industry has been trying to maintain itself entirely on the basis of "using telecommunications to support telecommunications," and has not received any subsidies from the national treasury. If we do not pay attention to business revenue, not only will the expansion plan not be able to be implemented, but even the current situation will not be able to be maintained. Therefore, within the scope of the law, the telegraph office has the right to sue in accordance with the law for anything that damages the telecommunications business. The various points of accusation made by the Guangchang Bureau, from the perspective of the telecommunications industry itself, are actually duties that must be fulfilled; otherwise, there will inevitably be acts of negligence of duty.

(3) The price of long-distance calls is generally calculated according to the call time and distance. The longer the call and the farther the distance, the more expensive the call. The Ministry-run long-distance telephone call price takes three minutes as the length and the spatial distance between the two places as the standard. Its purpose is to reduce the burden on the people. The prices in various places must be opened for business only after being approved by the Ministry of Transportation. This price is extremely low, only one-third of that in the United Kingdom and one-third of that in the United States. The Guangchang to Ningdu line is 70 kilometers long and the spatial distance is 50 kilometers. The charge for each call is three yuan, which is not excessive. The three-minute system is uniformly adopted for long-distance copper coin telephones run by the Ministry, and is an international system. The public who use long-distance telephones in various places in China have not heard of any inconvenience. The callers of long-distance telephones must have urgent matters to discuss, and the speaking must be simple and concise, and idle talk should be removed. In this way, the three-minute call time will naturally be enough. If there are complex matters that need to be discussed carefully, you can continue for three minutes. There is no reason to change the three-minute system to a five-minute system due to the need for a longer time for a small number of calls, thereby increasing the price standard and increasing the burden on the general caller. This is clear. However, if the telegraph office is too slow in handling long-distance telephone procedures, or if there are unsatisfactory points in the business, people from all walks of life can ask for improvements, and the telephone authorities are welcome.

(4) The telegraph office for the telecommunications transportation is the nerve system of a country. According to the law, it should be under the jurisdiction or supervision of the Ministry of Transportation, as mentioned above. However, the construction agencies of various provinces boast about local construction, and set up long-distance telephones in places where there are already Ministry-run long-distance telephones in various provinces. Not only are the parts and wires not in line with technical standards, but there is also no overall plan, resulting in the waste of public funds due to repeated construction or piecemeal construction. The reduction of call prices and competing with the Ministry's affiliated agencies for temporary profits is not allowed by law. In order to jointly develop the telephone business with the provincial governments, the Ministry of Transportation drew up the "Principles for the Ministry of Transportation to Entrust the Provincial Governments to Handle Long-Distance Telephones," which was approved by the Executive Yuan on July 7, 1933. If the Jiangxi construction authorities are really planning to develop the telephone transportation business, they should negotiate with the Jiangxi Telecommunications Administration to determine the method of entrustment, in order to comply with the law. Based on the above, the Guangchang County Government's communication with local agencies does have an effect of harming the revenue of the state-owned telephone business. The highway authority's opening of business telephone services between Nanfeng, Nancheng, Guangchang, and Ningdu is the same, and there is no basis in law. The Guangchang Telegraph Bureau truthfully reported it and asked for a ban, which is reasonable.

In short, telecommunications and transportation are the most needed construction undertakings at present. It is commendable that local agencies can work hard on this. However, to follow the central laws and regulations, communication system, and proceed step by step, both financial resources, manpower, and time will not be wasted, and the effect of a finger can be achieved. Otherwise, conflicts and disputes will be endless. Why should those who advocate construction do this?

Reduced Rates for Delayed News Telegrams to Various Parts of North America 231

According to news from the Ministry of Transportation, starting on December 1, the rates for delayed news telegrams (Lc press) transmitted via international radio or Great Eastern, Great Northern, and Pacific submarine cables to various parts of the United States and Canada will be reduced by eleven cents per word, and the Chinese mainline rates will also be revised from the same date.

Overview of Special Types of Long-Distance Telephone Calls 232

— Baozhen

The newly revised Domestic Long-Distance Telephone Business Regulations stipulate that long-distance telephone calls are divided into three types: call number communication, call person communication, and paging communication, as well as two categories: ordinary and expedited. To enhance the convenience of telephone calls for the public, three additional types of special calls are separately stipulated as follows:

(1) Special Contract Call: If a caller wishes to make a call between two designated telephone sets at a predetermined time on a specific date for a fixed period, they may enter into a special contract call agreement with the telephone bureau to ensure adherence. The effective period of this special contract call agreement must be at least one month, and the call fee must be paid in advance. After the calling user has entered into a special contract call with the telephone bureau, they can communicate with the other party at a specific time each day, saving the trouble of applying for registration on a case-by-case basis. Special contract calls are particularly convenient for businesses or exchanges that want to communicate with counterpart businesses in other locations at a specific time each day to report market conditions. This is because all types of long-distance telephone calls are prioritized based on registration order. It is difficult to predict when a long-distance telephone call registered through ordinary procedures can connect with the other party. Therefore, if a calling user wants to communicate with relevant businesses in other locations at a specific time each day, it is more convenient to use the special contract call mentioned above.

(2) Scheduled Call: A long-distance telephone call is called a scheduled call if the caller specifies a desired call time within the prescribed business hours when registering. If a caller wishes to use the scheduled call service, they must register with the telephone bureau in advance, a certain number of hours before the scheduled call time. The exact time will be stipulated and announced by the telephone bureau that offers this special service. The advantage of scheduled calls is that since the call time is predetermined, after the caller pays the fee and registers with the telephone bureau, they only need to go to make the call when the scheduled call time is approaching. If there are other important matters to attend to, they can go elsewhere, without wasting time waiting because they want to use a long-distance telephone.

(3) Night Call: A long-distance telephone call made during a specified period at night, where the call rate is lower than the daytime call rate, is called a night call. Previously, the Ministry of Transportation changed the long-distance telephone call calculation to be based on three-minute intervals. Furthermore, due to busy telephone lines during the day, the telephone bureau limited consecutive calls to three times, according to regulations. This was inconvenient for callers who needed to have longer conversations with the other party. For example, a news reporter stationed in Beijing might need a long-distance telephone call to report the news they gathered each day to a Shanghai newspaper office, which often required a lengthy conversation to complete the task. To meet the needs of the public and to unclog telephone traffic, the Ministry promulgated a measure to reduce the price of long-distance telephone calls at night. It stipulates that all calling users who make calls between 8:00 PM and 6:00 AM the next morning will be charged at a specific rate, which is approximately 30% lower than the daytime call rate. For example, if the ordinary daytime call rate from location A to location B is one yuan per call, the ordinary night call rate is only seventy cents. Furthermore, the expedited procedure can also be applied to night calls, with the fee being double the ordinary night call rate. Shanghai, Nanjing, Hangzhou, Zhenjiang, Wuxi, Wujin, and Wuxian were designated as the first seven locations for trial implementation, starting from December 1, 1935. After the new regulations are implemented, this measure will continue to be implemented, and efforts will be made to gradually extend it to other locations in the future.

If a caller uses the above-mentioned special contract calls and scheduled calls, and the long-distance telephone line is already occupied when the scheduled call time arrives, the telephone bureau will connect the call after the existing telephone conversation has ended, according to regulations. However, even if the caller has to wait slightly in such situations, it will only be a matter of minutes, and they should not feel too impatient.

The opening locations and detailed implementation measures for the above three special types of calls are to be reported by local telephone bureaus to the Ministry of Transportation for approval and then publicly announced for implementation based on social needs. Therefore, they cannot be universally implemented throughout the country at once. In the future, as long-distance telephone business develops gradually in various locations, if the telephone bureau finds that there is a need to open the above-mentioned calls, it can report to the Ministry of Transportation for approval at any time to facilitate the public.

Points to Note When Making Wireless Telephone Calls 233

(1) Please do not shake the handset while talking.

(2) When the other party is speaking, listen quietly and wait for them to finish a section before replying. Please do not interrupt to avoid both parties' voices becoming unintelligible.

(3) Please do not speak too softly or too loudly. The volume should be consistently moderate to ensure that the voice is clearer.
